тАШрдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореМ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рдирд╡рдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЧреЛрддрдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореНред рдЖрджрд┐рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдирд╡рдореНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ ред рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореМ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН – тАШ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореМ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд╛рдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореАрдпрдорд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдн рдЙрдкрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛ’ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпреЛрд╜рд╖реНрдЯрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА рд╡рд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореАрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╢реЛрд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛рдорд╛рджрд┐рддрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░ рдЛрдЪрдГ рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдгрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ- рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдорд╛рд╡рд┐рдордВ рд╕реБ рдореЗ рдпреБрд╡рдореЗрддрд╛рдирд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рд░реЛрдЪрдирд╛рдиреАрддрд┐ рддреГрдЪреМ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рей.рео) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

93
Agni and Soma
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
12 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ3, triс╣гс╣нubh 4тАУ8, g─Бyatr─л 9тАУ11, triс╣гс╣нubh 12
Another metrically complex hymn, this is the last attributed to Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa in Maс╣Зс╕Нala I. Despite the variety of meters, the piece is unified by the emphasis on the two gods to whom it is dedicated, and especially by the presence of the dvandva compound agn─л╠Б-с╣гo╠Бm─Б тАЬAgni and SomaтАЭ in every verse. This compound is found only twice elsewhere in the R╠еgveda (both times in Maс╣Зс╕Нala X). Although Agni and Soma are the quintessential ritual divinities, each representing a crucial sacrificial substance, this is the only hymn in the R╠еgveda explicitly dedicated to them together, and it is a fairly banal product. However, it is worth noting that, at least in our view, V.44, sometimes called the hardest hymn in the R╠еgveda, seems to concern Agni and Soma simultaneously, though it is identified in the Anukramaс╣З─л as an All God hymn.
The essential unity of the hymn is also discernible in its fairly simple thematic-cum-syntactic structure, which regularly constructs the verse as a rela tive clause referring to the actions of a pious mortal (тАЬwhoever serves [etc.]… тАЭ), and a main clause expressing his reward (see vss. 2тАУ3, 8, 10), as well as in repeated vocabulary in the earlier and later parts (see, e.g., matches between vss. 2 and 8, 3 and 10). The hymn also has an outer ring: the last word (12d ┼Ыruс╣гс╣нim├бntam тАЬhaving an attentive hearingтАЭ) recalls the first verb of the hymn (1b ┼Ыr╠ес╣Зutam), the imperative тАЬhear, listen!тАЭ
One part of the hymn stands out, verses 4тАУ6, which ascribe various mythological deeds to the pair. Curiously, the deeds in verses 4 and 5 are really more appropri ate to other gods: the mysterious Br╠еsaya and the theft in verse 4 are found also in a hymn to the river goddess Sarasvat─л (VI.61.1, 3), while verse 5 sounds like a generic praise of Indra. In verse 6, however, we do find mythological material appropriate to the two gods addressed, namely the story of the stealing of those gods. This is, tellingly, the only place in the hymn where the two gods are treated separately: M─Бtari┼Ыvan is the figure who stole fire, while the falconтАЩs theft of soma from heaven is also often alluded to.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, showerers (of desires), favourably hear this my invocation, graciously accept my hymns, and bestow felicity on the donor (of the oblation).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, hear this call of mine, you bulls.
Delight in the well-spoken hymns. Become refreshment for the
pious man.

Jamison Brereton Notes

BR corrected s├бm mahema to s├бm ahema тАШwe would bind togetherтАЩ to тИЪnah, an emendation accepted by Grassmann, Geldner, Oldenberg (tentatively), KEWA I.153. Although I also accepted it in Jamison 1983: 87, I now follow Got┼Н (1987: 243; accepted in EWA s.v.) in seeing it as a form of тИЪmah тАШbring aboutтАЩ, etymologically separate from тИЪmah тАШmagnifyтАЩ. Although I do not like multiplying entities, Got┼НтАЩs etymological connections look reasonable; an interpretation with тАШmake greatтАЩ is difficult; and a thematic pres. or aor. stem aha- to тИЪnah does not exist and the zero-grade (тЖР*nh╠е ) that would have to underlie it is not otherwise found to тИЪnah.

Griffith

AGNI and Soma, mighty Pair, graciously hearken to my call,
Accept in friendly wise my hymn, and prosper him who offers gifts.

Geldner

Agni und Soma, ihr Bullen, h├╢ret fein auf diesen Ruf von mir, nehmet die sch├╢nen Worte gut auf, seid dem Opferspender eine Freude!

Grassmann

O Agni-Soma, h├╢ret recht, ihr Stiere, diesen meinen Ruf; Die sch├╢nen Spr├╝che nehmet an, und seid zur Lust dem Opferer.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, grant to him who addresses this prayer to you both, store of cattle with sound strength and good horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, whoever today renders this speech as service for you two,
for him establish an abundance of heroes, the thriving of cattle, an
abundance of horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

y├бsmai тИЪyaj presents the classic parasmaipada configuration: тАЬsacrifice for someone else,тАЭ but ─Бy├бjase is resolutely middle. I do not have a good explanation for this beyond the fact that the functional distinction between act. y├бjati and mid. y├бjate is not well developed in the RV, esp. with preverb ─Б╠Б, and also that Agni, the subject, is essentially sacrificing to himself.

Although act. s─Б╠Бdhati can be transitive (and Witzel Got┼Н so tr. it), it also has intransitive/absolute uses (cf. the same tag in VI.70.3). Moreover, in this hymn s─Бdh├бyati (3a, 4c) serves as the transitive counterpart; the poet seems to have constructed an -ati /-├бyati Grundverb/Kaus. relationship.

Griffith

The man who honours you to-day, Agni and Soma, with this hymn,
Bestow on him heroic strength, increase of kine, and noble steeds.

Geldner

Agni und Soma! Der euch heute diese Rede weiht, dem bringet die Meisterschaft, Gedeihen der Rinder, Besitz guter Rosse!

Grassmann

O Agni-Soma, dem der heut mit diesem Liede euch verehrt, Dem reicht der Rinder Mehrung dar und reiche Schar an Ross und Mann.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, may he who offers you the oblation of clarified butter, enjoy sound strength, with progeny, through all his life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, whoever will piously perform a poured offering or the preparation of an oblation for you,
he along with his offspring will attain to an abundance of heroes and a complete lifespan.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A choppy series of clauses, five in the first three p─Бdas, with only the last dependent in any way on another.

Griffith

The man who offers holy oil and burnt oblations unto you,
Agni and Soma, shall enjoy great strength, with offspring, all his life.

Geldner

Agni und Soma! Wer euch eine Spende, wer euch eine Opferveranstaltung weiht, der soll mit seinen Nachkommen die Meisterschaft und das volle Lebensalter erreichen.

Grassmann

O Agni-Soma, wer mit Trank und Butterspende euch verehrt, Der m├╢g’ durch Kinder Heldenschar erreichen und des Lebens Ziel.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, that prowess of yours, by which you have carried off the cows that were the food of Paс╣Зi, is (well) known to us; you have slain the offspring of Bс╣Ыsya and you have obtained the luminary (the sun), for the benefit of the many.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bс╣Ыsayasya ┼Ыeс╣гa = Bс╣Ыsaya’s ─Бpatya, offspring (Nirukta, 3.2);

Bс╣Ыsaya = Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, an asura. The offspring of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б is Vс╣Ыtra. The agency of Agni and Soma in his death is explained by identifying them with the two vital airs, pr─Бс╣Зa and ap_na, the separation of which from Vс╣Ыtra was the possible cause of his death (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 2.5.2.4). By the destruction of Vс╣Ыtra, the enveloping cloud or gathered darkness, the sun was enabled to appear in the sky

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, this heroic deed of you two has become conspicuousтАФ that you stole the provender, the cows from the niggard.
You brought low the posterity of Br╠еsaya. You found the single light for the many.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, Bс╣Ыsaya, with his very non-Indo-Aryan name, and the destruction of his offspring are found elsewhere only in VI.61.3, a hymn devoted to Sarasvat─л. The theft of the provender (avas├б-) from the niggard (paс╣З├н-) is also found in that hymn, in vs. 1. The connection between the two hymns to different gods, found in different parts of the Saс╣Гhit─Б, is not clear to me, but the strong similarity of the passages at least that Bс╣Ыс╣гaya is a paс╣З├н-.

тАШрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдорд╣рдиреН рд╕реЛрд╜рдкреЛрд╜рднреНрдпрдореНрд░рд┐рдпрдд рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рдпрдиреНрдореЗрдзреНрдпрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрдВ рд╕рджреЗрд╡рдорд╛рд╕реАрддреНрддрджрдкреЛрджрдХреНрд░рд╛рдорддреН ’ ( рддреИ. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей. реи. рел. рез ) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддреЗрди рджреЛрд╖реЗрдг рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╛ рдирджреАрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрджреЛрд╖рд╛рджрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореМ рдореБрдХреНрддрд╡рдиреНрддреМ рее рд░реЛрдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ ред’ рд░реБрдЪ рджреАрдкреНрддреМ ред тАШ рдЕрдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддреЗрддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╣рд▓рд╛рджреЗрдГ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдпреБрдЪреН ред рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреВрдиреН ред’ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рджрдЯрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдкрд╛рджреЗ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдирдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд░реБрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЧреГрднреАрддрд╛рдиреН ред’ рд╣реГрдЧреНрд░рд╣реЛрд░реНрднрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рднрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou two, Agni and Soma, acting together, have sustained these constallations in the sky; you have liberated the rivers that had been defiled from the notorious imputation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: the imputation or brahmanicide refers to Indra’s killing of Vс╣Ыtra; the guilt is transferred to rivers, women and trees. Another legend: the rivers were defiled by the dead body of Vс╣Ыtra, which had fallen into them; the waters became unfit to bear any part in sacred rites, until they were purified by Agni and Soma, i.e. by oblations to fire and libations of Soma

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma and Agni, of like resolve, placed these lights in heaven. You, Agni and Soma, released from imprecation and from reproach the rivers that had been held back.

Jamison Brereton Notes

gop─Б╠Б(с╕е) in p─Бda a can be either sg. or pl. All the standard tr. take it as the former, referring to Agni, but this makes grammatical difficulties. Geldner interprets the following asya as a word-haplology for *asy *asy├б, thereby getting the 2nd sg. copula but gratuitously accenting the pronoun. Oldenberg reads *asy for asya and suggests accenting *c├бranti. Renou takes vi┼Ы─Б╠Бс╣Г gop─Б╠Б(с╕е) as a 3rd sg. expression (тАЬAgni est тАжтАЭ) and seems to leave the following text alone. But all such tr. must introduce an accent on whatever word they think follows the short initial clause, since, as it stands, two unaccented words, asya caranti, would open that clause. These difficulties can be avoided by interpreting gop─Б╠Бс╕е as plural, subject of caranti and coreferential with jant├бvaс╕е. Pl. gop─Б╠Б- is elsewhere used of AgniтАЩs sidekicks, presumably his flames, in VI.8.7. Though it is true that this same expression vi┼Ы─Б╠Бс╣Г gop─Б╠Б(с╕е) is found two hymns later (I.96.4) as an undoubted singular referring to Agni, the grammatical complications resulting from taking it as a singular here outweigh that argument for me.

Most tr. take the two-footed and four-footed as appositional to jant├бvaс╕е and therefore as those who roam by night. This is contrary to the usual RVic vision of the creatures settling down at night. AgniтАЩs flames make more sense as the roamers, evoking the flickering firelight that provides nightly illumination. The flames are called тАЬherdsmenтАЭ because people and animals gather around the fire then, like a flock. This interpretation does raise the question of how to construe the nom. case of that expression dvip├бc ca y├бd ut├б c├бtuс╣гpat. I take it as a definitional relative clause expanding on vi┼Ы─Б╠Бm (so also Oldenberg). The ca тАж ut├б is a mix of two тАЬboth тАж andтАЭ constructions: X ca Y ca and ut├б X ut├б Y, with the first half of the conjoined NP fronted around the subordinating y├бd. This construction is very similar to 9b d┼лr├й v─Б y├й ├бnti v─Б k├й cid, complete with the fronted first element.

The etymological relationship between citr├бс╕е and praket├бс╕е in c is not easily rendered in English.

Griffith

Agni and Soma, joined in operation ye have set up the shining lights in heaven.
From curse and from reproach, Agni and Soma, ye freed the rivers that were bound in fetters.

Geldner

Ihr beiden, Agni und Soma, setztet eines Sinnes diese Lichter an den Himmel. Ihr beide, Agni und Soma, habt die festgehaltenen Fl├╝sse aus Schimpf und Schande erl├╢st.

Grassmann

Sch├╢nwirkend setztet Agni ihr und Soma dort an den Himmel diese hellen Sterne; Ihr Agni-Soma l├╢stet vom Verderben und von der Schmach die festgehaltnen Str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, the wind brought one of you from heaven, a hawk carried off the other by force from the summit of the mountain; growing vast by praise, you have made the world wide for (the performance of) sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: V─Бyu brought Agni from heaven as desired by Bhс╣Ыgu, when performing a sacrifice. Soma was brought from svarga, on the summit of Mount Meru, by G─Бyatr─л, in the shape of a hawk. The allusion is to the early use of fire and Soma in ceremonies

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдореМ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╕реНрдп рд╣реЛрдорд╛рд░реНрдердорд╛рд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрд╕рдореАрдкрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ рдЗрджрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рд╡реАрддрдВ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддрдореН ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдЪ рд╣рд░реНрдпрддрдВ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛рдордпреЗрдерд╛рдореНред рд╣реЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдгрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рд░реМ рдЬреБрд╖реЗрдерд╛рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рдгрдВ рд╕реЗрд╡реЗрдерд╛рдореН ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╕реБрд╢рд░реНрдордгрд╛ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╕реБрдЦреМ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╣рд┐ рд╢реЛрднрдирд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреМ рдЪ рднреВрддрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рднрд╡рддрдореН ред рдЕрде рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрддреНрддрд╡рддреЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╢рдВ рд╢рдордиреАрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд░реЛрдЧрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рдордирдВ рдпреЛрдГ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рдирдВ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХрд░рдгрдВ рдЪ рдзрддреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрддреНрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реБрддрдореН ред рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХреЗрди- рд╢рдордирдВ рдЪ рд░реЛрдЧрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рдирдВ рдЪ рднрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдореН ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рек. реирез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рее рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ ред тАШ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдордгрдГ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареА ред рд╡реАрддрдореН ред тАШрд╡реА рдЧрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рдЬрдирдХрд╛рдиреНрддреНрдпрд╢рдирдЦрд╛рджрдиреЗрд╖реБ’ ред рдерд╕рд╕реНрддрдореН ред рдЕрджрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред рд╡реАрддрдВ рдЪ рд╣рд░реНрдпрддрдВ рдЪреЗрддрд┐ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рддреАрддреЗрдГ тАШрдЪрд╛рджрд┐рд▓реЛрдкреЗ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩреНрд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддреЗрд░реНрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ! рд╣рд░реНрдпрддрдореН ред рдкрд╛рджрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЬреБрд╖реЗрдерд╛рдореН ред рд╡реГрд╖рдгрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрд╕реНрдп тАШ рдЖрдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╡рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рддрд┐рдЩрдГ рдкрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рд╕реБрд╢рд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рд╛ ред рдЙрднрдпрддреНрд░ рдмрд╣реБрд╡реНрд░реАрд╣реМ тАШ рд╕реЛрд░реНрдордирд╕реА рдЕрд▓реЛрдореЛрд╖рд╕реА ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рднреВрддрдореН ред рд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ тАШ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, partake of the proffered oblation; be gracious to us; showerers (of desires), be plural ased; prosperous and diligent protectors, be propitious, and grant to the sacrificer health and exemption from illness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, the oblation set before youтАФpursue it; yearn for it, bulls; enjoy it.
Since you are providers of good shelter and good help, therefore
establish luck and lifetime for the sacrificer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The three imperatives in b, v─лt├бс╣Г h├бryatam тАж juс╣г├йth─Бm, all belong to roots that ordinarily take accusatives, yet all must be construed with the fronted gen. hav├нс╣гaс╕е pr├бsthitasya in p─Бda a. I donтАЩt quite understand the case syntax, but assume that these three verbs have been lumped together generically as verbs of consumption and enjoyment, for which gen. complements are often possible.

In c bh┼лt├бm can be either imperative or injunctive and is taken as injunctive in the published translation (as also by Geldner and Renou). However, since the immediately preceding hymn (I.92.15) contains the clausal diptych h├н + imperative, followed by ├бth─Б + imperative, exactly matching the structure here, I now think it would be better to interpret bh┼лt├бm as impv. here as well: тАЬBecome providers тАж, then establish тАжтАЭ (So Witzel Got┼Н.) An imperative interpretation also works better with the three abrupt imperatives that precede in b. For further disc. see comm. ad VII.99.3.

Griffith

Taste, Agni, Soma, this prepared oblation; accept it, Mighty Ones, and let it please you.
Vouchsafe us good protection and kind favour: grant to the sacrificer health and riches.

Geldner

Agni und Soma, verlanget, gel├╝stet nach dem vorgesetzten Opfer, ihr Bullen, la├Яt┬┤s euch munden! Ihr habt ja guten Schirm und Schutz, so bringet dem Opfernden Gl├╝ck und Heil!

Grassmann

Vom dargereichten Trank geniesst, o Stiere, o Agni-Soma, nehmt ihn an, erquickt euch; Denn ihr seid reich an Schutz und reich an H├╝lfe, drum schenkt nun auch dem Opfrer Heil und Segen.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ ! рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЬреЛ (рд╡реГрд╖рдгрд╛) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд (рд╕реБрд╢рд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд╛) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рд╕реБрдЦ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдорд╛) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдФрд░ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ (рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╕реНрдп) рджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рдГ) рд╣реЛрдореЗ рд╣реБрдП рдШреА рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЛ (рд╡реАрддрдореН) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ (рд╣рд░реНрдпреНрдпрддрдореН) рдкрд╛рддреЗ (рдЬреБрд╖реЗрдерд╛рдореН) рд╕реЗрд╡рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рдФрд░ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рднреВрддрдореН) рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рдЕрде) рдЗрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреАрдЫреЗ (рд╣рд┐) рдЗрд╕реА рдХрд╛рд░рдг (рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп) рдЬреАрд╡ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдЕрдирдиреНрдд (рд╢рдореН) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЛ (рдзрддреНрддрдореН) рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рддреЗ рддрдерд╛ (рдпреЛрдГ) рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрд▓рдЧ-рдЕрд▓рдЧ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЙрдкрдпреЛрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рд▓рд╛рдУ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рдЖрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рддрдиреЗ рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╣реЛрдореЗ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╕рдм рдкрд╡рди рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛ рдореЗрдШрдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдХреЗ рдЬрд▓ рдХреЛ рд╢реЛрдз рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рдЬреАрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЗ рд╣реЗрддреБ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░ рдзрд░реНрдо, рдЕрд░реНрде, рдХрд╛рдо рдФрд░ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░реЗ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпреМ рд╡реГрд╖рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд╢рд░реНрдореНрдорд╛рдгрд╛рд╜рдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╕реНрдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реЛ рд╡реАрддрдВ рд╣рд░реНрдпрддрдВ рдЬреБрд╖реЗрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╕рд╛ рднреВрддрдордереИрддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрдзрд┐ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╢рдВ рдзрддреНрддрдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреН рдпреЛрдГ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХреБрд░реБрддрд╕реНрддреМ рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЬрдпрдд рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, protect his sacrifice and defend him from illness, who, with a mind devoted to the gods, worships you with clarified butter and oblations; grant to the man engaged (in devotion) extreme felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever will serve Agni and Soma with an oblation, with a mind turned toward the gods, with ghee,
guard his (ritual) ordinance; protect him from narrow straits; to his clan, to his people extend great shelter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

sapary─Б╠Бt in b echoes sapary├бti in 2b, but displays the more usual case frame: acc. (god) + instr. (means of service). The instance in 2b takes acc. (means of service) + dat. (god), which is only otherwise found at X.37.1. The occurrence in this verse thus functions as a species of poetic repair.

Griffith

Whoso with oil and poured oblation honours, with God-devoted heart, Agni and Soma,–
Protect his sacrifice, preserve him from distress, grant to the sacrificer great felicity.

Geldner

Wer Agni und Soma mit Opfer ehrt, wer mit gottgerichtetem Denken, wer mit Schmalz, dessen Dienst nehmet beide in Obhut; sch├╝tzet ihn vor Not, gew├дhret dem Clane, dem Volk euren m├дchtigen Schutz!

Grassmann

Wer euch mit Trank, o Agni-Soma, ehret, mit gottergebnem Herzen, wer mit Butter, Ja, dessen Werk beschirmt ihr, sch├╝tzt ihn vor Gefahr, dem Haus, den Leuten reichet grossen Schutz ihr dar.

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, endowed with the like wealth, and invoked by a common invocation, share our praises, for you have (ever) been the chief of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Devatr─Б = deveс╣гu pra┼Ыastaс╕е; r─Бj─Бnau v─Б etau dev─Бn─Бm yad agniс╣гomau, Agni and Soma are they who are the two kings of the gods

Jamison Brereton

O Agni and Soma, who have common property and a common invocationтАФcrave our hymns.
You two have come together among the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The purport of the final p─Бda isnтАЩt clear to me, but it may indirectly comment on the unusual nature of the joint dedication of the hymn to these two gods.

Invoked together, mates in wealth, Agni-Soma, accept our hymns:
Together be among the Gods.

Agni and Soma, whoever piously honors you with this (oblation), who honors you with ghee,
for him shine loftily.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All standard tr. take b vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бsyeva te r├бvaс╕е as the main cl. to the y├бd cl.

beginning in a, while I take it as a part of that y├бd cl. There is no way to tell, since the second cl. lacks a verb whose accent or lack thereof would settle the matter.

There are also no semantic implications; I weakly prefer mine because of the fairly emphatic ─Б╠Бd тАШthen, just after thatтАЩ beginning the second hemistich.

All tr. take van├нnaс╕е as тАШtreesтАЩ (lit. тАШpossessing woodтАЩ). This is doubtless the primary sense here, since this sequence of vss. describes a forest fire, but тАШwinnersтАЩ is also possible, since the metaphorical context is that of a chariot race; see esp. 10a, 11c.

Jamison Brereton Notes

2nd du. d─лdayatam (10c) and jujoс╣гatam (11b) are somewhat problematic forms. They belong to redupl. thematic stems; other forms to these stems are subjunctives to the perfect. However, they have secondary endings, and the act. 2nd and 3rd du. subjunctive endings should be primary. Lubotsky identifies them as impvs. (Grassmann also jujoс╣гatam); K├╝mmel (35) treats them as тАЬhybridsтАЭ – morphologically belonging to the subjunctive but functioning as imperatives. They differ from some other secondarily thematized pf. impvs. in having full grade of the root syllable, like the subjunctive (versus zero-graade in p─лpyatam тИЪpi, тИЪv─Бvrdh├бsva тИЪvс╣Ыdh, etc. – but cf. pipr├бyasva тИЪpr─л). In the published translation they are treated as subjunctives (тАЬyou will shine,тАЭ тАЬyou will enjoyтАЭ), but they would might be better rendered as imperatives. For further disc. of such forms, see my forthcoming article on the perfect imperative. ## 094 Agni

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, bepleased with these our oblations, come to us together.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, you will enjoy these oblations of ours here.
Together drive right up to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply тАШmakesтАЩ on the basis of 9c sug├бс╣Г kс╣Ыdhi, though strictly speaking тАЬthat is an easy wayтАЭ is perfectly acceptable.

t─Бvak├б-, the vс╣Ыddhi derivative of the genitive of the 2nd ps. pronoun, enlarged with -ka-, is a striking form, though exactly what special effect it is aiming at is unclear. For the use of -ka- in pronominal derivatives, see Jamison 2009 (IIJ 52). As discussed there, the -ka- tends to signal a lower register or slangy tone.

10-11 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

2nd du. d─лdayatam (10c) and jujoс╣гatam (11b) are somewhat problematic forms. They belong to redupl. thematic stems; other forms to these stems are subjunctives to the perfect. However, they have secondary endings, and the act. 2nd and 3rd du. subjunctive endings should be primary. Lubotsky identifies them as impvs. (Grassmann also jujoс╣гatam); K├╝mmel (35) treats them as тАЬhybridsтАЭ – morphologically belonging to the subjunctive but functioning as imperatives. They differ from some other secondarily thematized pf. impvs. in having full grade of the root syllable, like the subjunctive (versus zero-graade in p─лpyatam тИЪpi, тИЪv─Бvrdh├бsva тИЪvс╣Ыdh, etc. – but cf. pipr├бyasva тИЪpr─л). In the published translation they are treated as subjunctives (тАЬyou will shine,тАЭ тАЬyou will enjoyтАЭ), but they would might be better rendered as imperatives. For further disc. of such forms, see my forthcoming article on the perfect imperative. ## 094 Agni

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni and Soma, cherish our horses, and may our cows, affordin g(milk that yields butter for) oblations, be well nourished; give to us, who are affluent, strength (to perform) religious rites, and make our sacrifice productive of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni and Soma, deliver our steeds (to safety). Let the ruddy (cows) who sweeten the oblations swell up.
In us and in our benefactors establish powers. Give our ceremony an attentive hearing.

Most of the next 22 hymns (94тАУ115) are attributed to Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa by the Anukramaс╣З─л. Though a few (99тАУ100, alternatively 105) have other poets named, the presence of the Kutsa refrain in both 100 and 105 (99 is a one-verse hymn) supports the unity of the collection. The Kutsa refrain, in triс╣гс╣нubh, тАЬThis let Mitra and Varuс╣Зa grant to us, and Aditi, River, and Earth and Heaven,тАЭ occupies the last hemistich of the last verse of every hymn except I.97 (a g─Бyatr─л hymn), 99 (a one-verse hymn), and 104 (though this last hymn is in triс╣гс╣нubh).
The Agni hymns (94тАУ99) are each dedicated to a different form of Agni. There follow, in the normal order, five hymns to Indra, three to the All Gods, with miscel laneous other divinities making up the collection. The collection is at a generally high level of poetic craftsmanship, but we will only single out for special mention 104, a challenging Indra hymn, 105, a famous and enigmatic All God hymn, and the lovely Dawn hymn 113.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most tr. take Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as the objects of dh─Б╠Бyase: approx. тАЬAgni is for the suckling of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa.тАЭ But Agni is the one more likely in need of suckling (that is, feeding the fire); cf., e.g., II.5.7. In particular, in the next hymn, I.95.1, Agni is the object of the transitive/causative dh─Бpayete. I therefore take the gen. mitr├бsya v├бruс╣Зasya as dependent on h├йс╕╖aс╕е in b, parallel to mar├║t─Бс╣Г. h├йс╕╖a(s)- is characteristic of Varuс╣Зa (cf. I.24.14, VII.84.2; in VII.62.4 Mitra is included).

avay─Бt─Б╠Бm is the problem in the second p─Бda. Most tr. take it as a 3rd sg.

imperative (e.g., Renou тАЬquтАЩil exorciseтАЭ), but if so, it must be a middle root pres.

imperative, and there are no middle forms to this root тИЪy─Б (as opposed to тИЪy─Б тАШimploreтАЩ). There is also the problem that the form should not be accented on the stem but on the preverb (*├бva y─Бt─Бm; see Geldner n. 12b). Lubotsky appears to take it as a gen. pl. of the act. part. to the root pres., but in the absence of a tr. it is hard to know how he would interpret it in context. Best to follow Oldenberg (who follows BR) in emending to

*avay─Бt─Б╠Б, the nom. sg. agent noun. Renou is tempted by this reading, save for the fact that with the acc. complement h├йс╕╖aс╕е we should expect the accent ├бvay─Бt─Б. However, the тАЬruleтАЭ about the case of complements to agent nouns is broken so often that this objection is not cogent. The final -m could have been acquired from the following mar├║t─Бm (so Oldenberg), and since тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ is a characteristic Marut verb and a genuine example of the gen. pl. part. y─Бt─Б╠Бm is used of the Maruts in the refrain V.55.1-9, it may have been rhetorically natural to transform the agent noun into this participle.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдорд╛) рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╣реЗрддреВ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рдпреВ рдЗрд╡ (рдкрд┐рдкреГрддрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдкрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрддреНрддрдореН (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ) рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЖ) (рдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ (рдЙрд╕реНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдГ) рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╕реВрджрдГ) рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рджреБрдЧреНрдзрд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдХреНрд╖рд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐) (рдордШрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рд╡рд╛ (рдзрддреНрддрдореН) рдзрд░рддрдореН (рдХреГрдгреБрддрдореН) рдХреБрд░реБрддрдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░рдореН) рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН (рд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдордиреНрддрдореН) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдВ рдмрд╣реБрд╕реБрдЦрд╣реЗрддреБрдореН рее резреи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдирд╣рд┐ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдХрд╕реНрдпрдЪрд┐рджреНрдмрд▓рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреА рдЬрд╛рдпреЗрддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрддреЗ рд╕реБрд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрд╖реВрдкрдпреЛрдЬрдиреАрдпреЗ рее резреи реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреЛрд░реНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рд╖рд╖реНрдард╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдпреИрдХреЛрдирддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдореЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГред рдкреНрд░рдердордордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрдирд╡рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рд╡рд╛рдпреВ рд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрд╢рд┐рд╡рд╛рдп рдХреБрдгрд╛рдЪреЗ рдмрд│ рд╡рд╛рдврдд рдирд╛рд╣реА рд╡ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреА рд╣реЛрдд рдирд╛рд╣реА. рддреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдЙрдкрдпреЛрдЧ рдХрд░реВрди рдШреЗрддрд▓рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резреи рее
